## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship of a material. Temperature typically modifies elastic stiffness, yield behavior, and can introduce thermal softening or thermally activated deformation mechanisms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (linear elastic): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear stress-strain at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 + c2 * T) (elastic modulus varying linearly with temperature)
- Thermal softening linear: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * T) (linear thermal correction to stiffness)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (nonlinear stress-strain curve, strain hardening)
- Temperature-dependent power-law: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 + c3 * T) (power-law hardening with thermal dependence)
- Ramberg-Osgood type: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic + plastic hardening)
- Johnson-Cook type (no strain rate): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T) (hardening with thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook thermal softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T**c4) (power-law thermal softening)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 * T) (Arrhenius-like thermal modulus reduction)
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) (saturating stress-strain curve)
- Voce with temperature: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) * (1 + c2 * T) (saturating hardening with thermal effect)
- Ludwik model: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Thermally activated flow: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (thermally activated deformation)
- Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (polynomial constitutive law)
- Combined model: sigma = (c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(c3 * T) (general hardening with exponential thermal softening)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Elastic-to-plastic transition → piecewise or smooth combination of linear term (c0*epsilon) and power-law term (c1*epsilon**c2)
- Thermal softening of modulus → multiplicative factor (1 - c*T) or (1 + c*T) with c<0, reflecting decreasing stiffness with temperature
- Arrhenius-type thermal activation → exp(c1 / T) or exp(c1 * T) factors multiplying mechanical response, common in creep and diffusion-controlled deformation
- Stress saturation at large strains → (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) form indicating asymptotic approach to maximum stress (Voce-type behavior)
- Separable temperature and strain dependence → sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T), where mechanical and thermal responses are multiplicatively separable
- Strain hardening exponent sensitivity → power-law exponent c in epsilon**c typically between 0 and 1 for metals, indicating diminishing hardening rate
- Melting/critical temperature behavior → factors like (1 - c0*T**c1) that drive stress to zero at a critical temperature
- Concavity change in stress-strain → presence of both epsilon and epsilon**2 terms or competing exponential terms indicating inflection in hardening behavior
